Here for the antique flea market, fun to walk and see some of the creative  one of a kinds you can find here. However,  there was one selling benches that were made with a 2x6, simple all the way, $175. No. For a little more another vendor had gorgeous natural wood, sturdy top and legs. Wish I'd taken a photo. Definitely a must see place to go. Third Sunday of the month, wear comfortable shoes and sunscreen with a hat.</Review>

<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< text>
The school is decent. Decent people, great teachers and good luck getting parking (park at the stadium for the first week or two if you drive. If someone is dropping you off, try going early. Around 7:30 is when traffic starts).

What I want to inform new students is the financial aid office is horrible at explaining how the FASFA works with new students, some did not even have the patience. I would suggest calling a representative through the FASFA website. They have more patience and you don't have to get in line multiple times (I did that a lot in freshman year).

The food at the cafeteria from what I remember was okay. The food was also overpriced. If you can, go to the food bank on campus. The nurse's office also has snacks but you can only grab one item. If you have the funds, there are restaurants nearby. Also, if you can and have the funds, go buy a pizza and share with others. (You have no idea how much other students or friends appreciate it).

Lastly, don't forget to say hello and good morning to everyone. Teachers are nicer to you and it helps break the ice for other students.< /text>

<Review>My wife and I visited Menlo Park one Sunday when we happened to be in the bay area (we live in the central valley, but if we could we would attend here!).  This is a church where a lot of good things are happening!  We attended both a contemporary and traditional service, and both were outstanding.  We went to the main church, but there are apparently a variety of options, depending upon your preference. Music was awesome.  This is a big church building, but strategically placed screens made it so everyone has a good view of what is going on. John Ortberg was preaching when we came, and you will have to search far and wide to find another who will compare with this speaker.  Ortberg is articulate and inspiring. Following the service he prayed for us and a number of other individuals that came forward after the service.  He is not only a gifted speaker but author of a number of best selling books.

There is a lot going on here with children's ministries for families with children.   People were friendly and accepting.  The director of small groups and a number of other ministries greeted us and spent quite a while talking with us, explaining the various ministries of the church.  If you are from the bay area you have the wonderful opportunity to grow in the influence of this wonderful church body.  If not, you will have to content yourself with watching their sermons online as I do.</Review><Pics>None<//Pics><response>None<//response>< gmap_id>

<text>The perfect store for party planners!  Dollar Tree is famous for Dollar Deals but if you are planning a party this is the store for you. They have a very large selection of party items like napkins, hats, streamers, cards, wrapping paper, glasses, cups, tablecloths, balloons and more. if you are a bargain hunter Dollar Tree Never Let You Down. A good tip is to make sure you look at expiration dates and for dented items when shopping for food but you will always get your dollars worth here.  The Dollar Tree in Indio California is very clean and well-staffed. I shop there early in the morning and never have to wait very long at the checkout. This is the place to get great greeting cards as well. They have a very large selection and most items are  two for a dollar.  I can't really recommend buying kitchen supplies here except for garbage bags, Ziploc bags and items like foil. These are great deals to get at the Dollar Tree. They do not have a big variety of fresh food items but you can buy great spices and canned goods at low prices.</text>< user_name>

< review>
Excellent workout. Straight up the fire service road for about 3 miles. Best to go early before the sun comes out strong since the road is fully exposed and has very little shade. Take plenty of water because it is not available once you get there. Keep in mind a 90 degree will sap your energy and hydration is a must. It takes about an hour to get up to Henninger Flats give or take a few minutes.</review>

<username>Bradley Martin<//username>< resp>
None</resp>
<Text>It's a great place to hike to from Eaton Canyon... If you're NEW pay attention! There is a "contributor" Tatiana Lopez that appears to have uploaded 2500+ photos and tagged them as being taken at Henninger Flats. They are NOT properly tagged... and I've exhausted reported as many as I can... but it will take forever! So just ignore her photos... there is a very obvious difference in her photos verses what others have posted/tagged.

For those Hiking up from Eaton Canyon... it is a challenging elevation climb, but an easy hike as the trail is quite clear and wide. The trail is the "fire road" that leads up to Henninger (which was repaired a number of years ago after a landslide took out large portions of the road (and mountain side)... I'm glad it was reopened... and for those wanting a big challenge you can continue up to Mt. Wilson if you're feeling bold!

Remember to "leave no trace" and keep your 10 essentials with you. This is still wild country with spiders, snakes, bears and mountain lions in the area. So please, don't treat your hike as if you're going to Tom Sawyer Island and Disneyland. You can get hurt if you're not being safe. People have fallen from ledges and been hurt (a few killed) so treat nature with respect and stay firmly on the trails.

YIS,
-Bradley<//Text>< Pics>
None< /Pics>

Joshua & Darby</username>
< Review>
In May I made the move from Seattle to Los Angeles and it didn‚Äôt take long for me to start itching to get outdoors and explore. Unfortunately it took me a couple weeks to settle in and finally make time to get out. I started doing some research on recommended places to camp near LA and Henniger Flats was at the top of almost everyone‚Äôs list that I could find online. A short hike, free camping and not far from where I live; sold. Especially for my first camping adventure since making the move to sunny California.

Henniger Flats is located in the San Gabriel Mountains near Altadena, California. Directions on getting there are pretty simple coming from downtown LA.

The trailhead to Henniger Flats is located off N Altadena Drive. It‚Äôs not easy to spot but if you‚Äôre familiar with the area, you‚Äôll probably have no problem finding it. If you‚Äôre heading to Henniger Flats for the night, you‚Äôll have to pay attention to where you park because there‚Äôs not a lot of overnight or long-term parking at the trailhead. I personally parked down the street on N Altadena in the neighborhood. Just keep an eye out for parking signs and you‚Äôll probably be ok.

When you reach the trailhead you‚Äôll see a sign that reads, ‚ÄúThe Henniger Flats Project.‚Äù You have to hike up  Mount Wilson Toll Road to get there. Initially it‚Äôs a little confusing to figure out which trail you need to be on to get there, at least it was for me. You‚Äôll walk down the beginning of the trail and cross the white bridge. Once you cross the white bridge, stay to the left and head up until you reach Henniger Flats. It‚Äôs about a 3 mile hike and the incline gets steep at times. There are plenty of benches to rest at on the way up.

There‚Äôs no shade on the way up so it‚Äôs important to start your hike early if you intend on camping and have a heavy pack. Also bring an abundance of water. There is a visitor center and museum at Henniger Flats, but there‚Äôs no running water. Be prepared! I didn‚Äôt run into any wildlife and you probably won‚Äôt either since the trail is very popular and there seems to be a lot of foot traffic throughout the day. There are a few signs for rattlesnakes but I didn‚Äôt run into any.

After your 3 mile journey to the top, you‚Äôve reached Henniger Flats. First thing‚Äôs first, you need to find the onsite LACFD Forester that‚Äôs on duty to check in. I read that you‚Äôll be given a permit for camping and to use a stove, but I didn‚Äôt have to do that when I checked in for whatever reason. There was a cub scout clan doing some work at the campgrounds so I‚Äôm sure he was busy and distracted. After or even before you check in, you can check out the visitor center and museum to learn about Henniger Flats and the surrounding areas. It‚Äôs pretty neat.

Once you get checked in you‚Äôll have to find your camping lot. There are 3 levels of camping at Henniger Flats. There‚Äôs a lower level campground near the visitor center and museum. It seemed pretty busy, so I walked to the upper and Fiji campgrounds. The forester actually recommended the Fiji campground area for a quieter environment and great place for setting up hammocks. He was absolutely right and if you‚Äôre looking for a quiet place to chillax, Fiji is the way to go.

Most larger camping lots have picnic tables and stoves to cook on. It‚Äôs worth noting there are about 15-20 camping lots in the upper and lower campgrounds. Fiji only has 3 camping lots, so you have to get there early to snag one. You can also call the forester head of time to get some insight on open camp lots. There‚Äôs plenty of shade once you get settled and the campgrounds are very well kept. There was no trash, the trails were well maintained and the views are phenomenal. There‚Äôs plenty of trails to check out after you get settled in.

Overall I had a great experience camping at Henniger Flats and I will certainly go again. #LosAngeles #Hiking #Outdoors<//Review>

I ordered the steak and eggs. To begin with the service was great and Cristi was the bomb. Reason i say this is because, i had a situation with my dinner plate. I advised Cristi of my situation and she apologized and cleared our table. But to my amazement she immidiately escalated my concern. The manager came over and apologized personal and asked if i would like anything to replace my meal, i said no thank you. When we asked for the check, the manager had discounted my meal off the check. Yes, i had a situation with my meal but it was quickly handled by Marissa. That left me with a good feeling and i would definitely come back and recommend Mimi's to everyone. Simply on the fact that they approciate my being a customer.<//Review>

< text>
Having a early breakfast on Friday morning before Fontana's NASCAR events this past weekend, I was incredibly impressed. Having been loyal to this restaurant in past for years, was ready to give it up. Why? Overall menu was extensively with 'unhealthy' dishes as if was still Dean Evans owned and operated. Asked the waiter Javier, whom was fabulous as a server to request the cook to minimize as much as possible the oil/grease used to 'fry' their breakfast potato's. He sated that he would attempt. Voila, great potatoes as Mimi's is branded in servings, was terrific. Without oil at ALL! So so good. Complimented the Great General Manager Chris on the order request outcome. He shared with me that Mimi's was owned now by a large Global entity and had more healthy training in the cooking/recipes. Finally</text>
